      <h3><span id="Return_to_the_backbenches_.282010.E2.80.932015.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_the_backbenches_(2010–2015)">Return to the backbenches (2010–2015)</span></h3> 
      <p>On 13 May 2010, in his first public appearance since leaving <a href="/wiki/10_Downing_Street" title="10 Downing Street">10 Downing Street</a>, two days after resigning as Prime Minister and Leader of the Labour Party, Brown confirmed he intended to stay on in Parliament, serving as a Labour <a href="/wiki/Backbencher" title="Backbencher">backbencher</a>, to serve the people of his <a href="/wiki/Kirkcaldy_and_Cowdenbeath_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Kirkcaldy and Cowdenbeath (UK Parliament constituency)">Kirkcaldy and Cowdenbeath constituency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC13May2010Backbencher_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC13May2010Backbencher-128">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Towards the end of May 2010, Brown began writing <i><a href="/wiki/Beyond_the_Crash" title="Beyond the Crash">Beyond the Crash</a></i>, completing it after 14 weeks. The book discusses the 2007–08 financial crisis and Brown's recommendations for future co-ordinated global action.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>He played a prominent role in the lead-up to, and the aftermath of, the <a href="/wiki/2014_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="2014 Scottish independence referendum">2014 Scottish independence referendum</a>, campaigning for Scotland to stay in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 1 December 2014, Brown announced that he would not be seeking re-election to parliament. He stood down at the general election in May 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IMF_speculation">IMF speculation</span></h3> 
      <p>In April 2011, media reports linked Brown with the role as the next managing director of the International Monetary Fund following the scheduled retirement of <a href="/wiki/Dominique_Strauss-Kahn" title="Dominique Strauss-Kahn">Dominique Strauss-Kahn</a>. Brown's successor and Leader of the Opposition, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Miliband" title="Ed Miliband">Ed Miliband</a>, supported Brown for the role while the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, voiced opposition to this.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Following the arrest of Strauss-Kahn for alleged sexual assault in May 2011, and his subsequent resignation, these reports re-surfaced.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Support for Brown among economists was mixed but British Government backing for his candidature was not forthcoming and instead supported <a href="/wiki/Christine_Lagarde" title="Christine Lagarde">Christine Lagarde</a> – the eventual successful candidate – for the post.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_appointments">Other appointments</span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tim_Berners-Lee" title="Tim Berners-Lee">Sir Tim Berners-Lee</a>, who had worked with the government during Brown's premiership to publish government data on the internet in the <a href="/wiki/Data.gov.uk" title="Data.gov.uk">data.gov.uk</a> project, subsequently invited Brown to become a board director of the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Foundation" title="World Wide Web Foundation">World Wide Web Foundation</a> to "advise the Web Foundation on ways to involve disadvantaged communities and global leaders in the development of sustainable programs that connect humanity and affect positive change".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> On 22 April 2011 it was announced that Brown would be taking on an unpaid advisory role at the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Brown was also appointed as the inaugural 'Distinguished Leader in Residence' by <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> and has already taken part in discussions and lectures relating to the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">global financial crisis</a><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> and globalisation.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In July 2012 Brown was named by Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Special_Envoy_of_the_Secretary-General" title="Special Envoy of the Secretary-General">Special Envoy</a> on Global Education. He chaired the <a href="/wiki/International_Commission_on_Financing_Global_Education_Opportunity" title="International Commission on Financing Global Education Opportunity">International Commission on Financing Global Education Opportunity</a>. The position is unpaid.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 2015, Brown took his first large-scale role in the private sector since standing down as prime minister in 2010, becoming an advisor to <a href="/wiki/PIMCO" title="PIMCO">PIMCO</a>. Any money earned from the role is to go to the Gordon and Sarah Brown Foundation to support charitable work.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poverty">Poverty</span></h3> 
      <p>Brown is concerned about child poverty and poverty in general. Brown said, “It makes me angry. I’m seeing poverty I didn’t think I would ever see again in my lifetime. Slum housing was a feature of my childhood in the 1950s and 1960s, and I thought we had finally got over the worst of child poverty. Tax credits were the key to that.” Brown also said, “You can’t solve child poverty with the existing system. <a href="/wiki/Universal_credit" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal credit">Universal credit</a> is completely underfunded and every time they move people on to it you see more poverty. Minimum wage jobs don’t pay enough to keep a family with two or three children out of poverty.” Brown said further, “The government is trying to analyse this as people who are too lazy to get into work. But the problem is that people can’t earn enough to stay out of poverty.”<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span></h2> 
      <p>The 2003 TV movie <a href="/wiki/The_Deal_(2003_film)" title="The Deal (2003 film)">The Deal</a> followed Tony Blair's rise to power, and his friendship and rivalry with Gordon Brown. Brown was portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Ian_Grieve" title="Ian Grieve">Ian Grieve</a> in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a> television film <a href="/wiki/Coalition_(film)" title="Coalition (film)"><i>Coalition</i></a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gordon_and_Sarah_Brown.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gordon_and_Sarah_Brown.jpg/220px-Gordon_and_Sarah_Brown.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gordon_and_Sarah_Brown.jpg/330px-Gordon_and_Sarah_Brown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gordon_and_Sarah_Brown.jpg/440px-Gordon_and_Sarah_Brown.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3448" data-file-height="2332"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gordon_and_Sarah_Brown.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Sarah Brown attending one of her husband's speeches
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Brown's early girlfriends included the journalist <a href="/wiki/Sheena_McDonald" title="Sheena McDonald">Sheena McDonald</a> and <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margareta_of_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="Princess Margareta of Romania">Princess Margarita</a>, the eldest daughter of exiled <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_of_Romania" title="Michael I of Romania">King Michael of Romania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GBStory_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GBStory-30">[30]</a></sup> At the age of 49, Brown married <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Jane_Brown" title="Sarah Jane Brown">Sarah Macaulay</a> in a private ceremony at his home in <a href="/wiki/North_Queensferry" title="North Queensferry">North Queensferry</a>, Fife, on 3 August 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> On 28 December 2001 a daughter, Jennifer Jane, was born prematurely and died on 7 January 2002 one day after suffering a <a href="/wiki/Brain_haemorrhage" class="mw-redirect" title="Brain haemorrhage">brain haemorrhage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> They have two sons, John Macaulay (born 17 October 2003)<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> and (James) Fraser (born on 18 July 2006). In November 2006, Fraser was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Cystic_fibrosis" title="Cystic fibrosis">cystic fibrosis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> had learned of the situation in 2006 and published the story. In 2011 Brown stated he had wanted the details of his son's condition kept private and that the publication had left him "in tears".<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The <i>Sun</i> said they approached Brown and that discussion occurred with his colleagues who provided quotes to use in the article.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Sarah Brown rarely makes official appearances, whether with or without her husband.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> She is patron of several charities and has written articles for national newspapers related to this.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> At the 2008 Labour Party Conference, Sarah caused surprise by taking to the stage to introduce her husband for his keynote address.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> Since then her public profile has increased.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_17_July_2009_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_17_July_2009-153">[153]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brown has two brothers, John Brown and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Brown_(media_strategist)" title="Andrew Brown (media strategist)">Andrew Brown</a>. Andrew has been Head of Media Relations in the UK for the French-owned utility company <a href="/wiki/EDF_Energy" title="EDF Energy">EDF Energy</a> since 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-154">[154]</a></sup> Brown is also the brother-in-law of environmental journalist <a href="/wiki/Clare_Rewcastle_Brown" title="Clare Rewcastle Brown">Clare Rewcastle Brown</a>. Brown wrote a piece for <i>The Independent</i> supporting Clare's current environmental efforts on behalf of <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Independent_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-155">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Whilst Prime Minister, Brown spent some of his spare time at <a href="/wiki/Chequers" title="Chequers">Chequers</a>, the house often being filled with friends. The Browns have entertained local dignitaries like Sir Leonard Figg.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Brown is also a friend of Harry Potter author <a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a>, who says of Brown "I know him as affable, funny and gregarious, a great listener, a kind and loyal friend."<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brown is a strong supporter of the NHS partly due to both the experimental surgery that saved the sight in his right eye after his retina became detached, and the care he and Sarah Brown received when their premature firstborn baby died. Blindness in his left eye resulting in his lack of peripheral vision contributed to Brown's supposed antisocial nature and awkward public manner. For example, both on a podium and before a camera, while reading "he needs to look slightly to one side of the paper in order to focus; when speaking to an audience or into a camera lens, he must remember to correct what would normally be an automatic tendency to look slightly askew in order to see clearly with his good eye". Brown's papers were prepared in capital letters and in extremely large type, resulting in his stack of papers at the dispatch box being noticeably bulky due to fewer words per page. Former staffers often attributed Brown's outbursts of temper in Downing Street to his frustration with his physical limitations.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Brown is a noted supporter of Kirkcaldy-based football club <a href="/wiki/Raith_Rovers_F.C." title="Raith Rovers F.C.">Raith Rovers</a> and has written articles about his relationship with the club.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <p>The son of a <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> <a href="/wiki/Minister_(Christianity)" title="Minister (Christianity)">minister</a>, Brown has talked about what he calls his "<a href="/wiki/Moral_compass" class="mw-redirect" title="Moral compass">moral compass</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> and of his parents being his "inspiration".<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> He has, at least ostensibly, been keen to keep his religion a private matter.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> According to <i>The Guardian</i>, he is a member of the Church of Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span id="Titles.2C_honours_and_awards"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles,_honours_and_awards">Titles, honours and awards</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Styles_of_address">Styles of address</span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>1951–1982: <i>Mr</i> James Gordon Brown</li> 
       <li>1982–1983: <i><a href="/wiki/PhD" class="mw-redirect" title="PhD">Dr</a></i> James Gordon Brown<sup id="cite_ref-values_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-values-167">[167]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>1983–1996: <i>Dr</i> James Gordon Brown <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of the British House of Commons">MP</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>1996–2015: <i><a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Privy Council of the United Kingdom">The Right Honourable</a> Dr</i> James Gordon Brown <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of the British House of Commons">MP</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-Privy_Counsellor_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Privy_Counsellor-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sworn_of_the_Privy_Council_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sworn_of_the_Privy_Council-170">[170]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>2015–2018: <i>The Right Honourable Dr</i> James Gordon Brown<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>2018–present: <i>The Right Honourable Dr</i> James Gordon Brown <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Honorary_Fellow_of_the_Royal_Society_of_Edinburgh" class="mw-redirect" title="Honorary Fellow of the Royal Society of Edinburgh">HonFRSE</a></span><sup id="cite_ref-HonFRSE_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HonFRSE-172">[172]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Honorary_Degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Honorary Degree">Honorary Degree</a> (D.Univ) from <a href="/wiki/Brunel_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Brunel University">Brunel University</a> (1996)<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Honoris_Causa" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctor Honoris Causa">Doctor Honoris Causa</a> (Hon.Dr.) from <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a> (2003)<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Honorary <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Laws" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctor of Laws">Doctor of Laws</a> (LL.D.) from <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gordon_University" title="Robert Gordon University">Robert Gordon University</a> (2003)<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Honorary <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Humane_Letters" title="Doctor of Humane Letters">Doctor of Humane Letters</a> (D.H.L.) from <a href="/wiki/New_York_University" title="New York University">New York University</a> (2005)<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Honorary <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Civil_Law" title="Doctor of Civil Law">Doctor of Civil Law</a> (D.C.L.) from <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a> (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Honorary <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Letters" title="Doctor of Letters">Doctor of Letters</a> (D.Litt.) from <a href="/wiki/University_of_Delhi" title="University of Delhi">University of Delhi</a> (2008)<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Honoris_Causa" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctor Honoris Causa">Doctor Honoris Causa</a> (Hon.Dr.) from <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a> (2015)<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Elected an Honorary Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_Edinburgh" title="Royal Society of Edinburgh">Royal Society of Edinburgh</a> (2018)<sup id="cite_ref-HonFRSE_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HonFRSE-172">[172]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>In March 2009 Brown was named <a href="/wiki/Appeal_of_Conscience_Foundation#World_Statesman_of_the_Year" title="Appeal of Conscience Foundation">World Statesman of the Year</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Appeal_of_Conscience_Foundation" title="Appeal of Conscience Foundation">Appeal of Conscience Foundation</a>, an American organisation 'dedicated to promoting peace, human rights and understanding between <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religious faiths</a>'. The award was presented by <a href="/wiki/Rabbi" title="Rabbi">Rabbi</a> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Schneier" title="Arthur Schneier">Arthur Schneier</a> who praised Brown's "compassionate leadership in dealing with the challenging issues facing humanity, his commitment to freedom, human dignity and the environment, and for the major role he has played in helping to stabilise the world's financial system".<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> </p>
